Founded in 1997 by Martin Gonzalez as a claim adjudication company, the company launched its software division in 2000 with a product called MD2000, a healthcare practice management application. That product evolved into MDVita, their current ONC-certified EHR and practice management suite. The company describes itself as having \"more than 20 years of service in South Florida\" and emphasizes low employee turnover (average tenure of 10 years).\n     9→\n    10→Health Care 2000 services \"hundreds of medical centers\" according to their website, primarily in South Florida. Their niche is value-based care providers — specifically physicians operating under risk-based contracts with Medicare Advantage plans and other value-driven payment arrangements. Beyond software, the company provides customized financial consulting and data analysis services through in-house healthcare finance professionals. The company has no presence on major software review platforms (G2, Capterra) and appears to be a small regional vendor serving a localized market.\n    11→\n    12→## Product: MDVita\n    13→\n    14→CHPL ID: 11000\n    15→CHPL Product Number: 15.04.04.2904.MDVi.27.02.1.221020\n    16→Version: 27 (certified October 20, 2022, by Drummond Group)\n    17→SED Intended Users: Family Practice\n    18→\n    19→### What It Is\n    20→\n    21→MDVita is an ONC-certified electronic medical record (EMR) and physician practice management application. It is not a component of a larger product — MDVita is the full product, encompassing both clinical EHR and administrative practice management functionality in a single integrated suite. The product is specifically designed for value-based care providers in primary/family practice settings.\n    22→\n    23→MDVita Analytics is a separately named extension module that provides financial analytics and utilization performance measurement. It appears to be offered as an add-on to the core MDVita product.\n    24→\n    25→The product has a broad certification profile with 38+ criteria including clinical documentation (a)(1)–(a)(5), (a)(12), (a)(14), transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(2), patient portal/VDT (e)(1), public health reporting (f)(1)–(f)(2), FHIR API (g)(7)–(g)(10), and Direct messaging (h)(1). This is a comprehensive certification for a small vendor.\n    26→\n    27→### Users & Market\n    28→\n    29→**Target users**: Physicians and clinical staff in family/general/primary care practices. The SED testing report indicates the intended user is \"Family Practice.\"\n    30→\n    31→**Customer base**: \"Hundreds of medical centers\" in South Florida, per the vendor website. The product is described as \"a very popular application suite used in South Florida by many health care providers\" (Alignable profile). No specific customer names or case studies are publicly available.\n    32→\n    33→**Clinical setting**: Ambulatory primary care practices, particularly those operating under Medicare Advantage risk-based contracts and value-based payment arrangements. Not hospital-oriented.\n    34→\n    35→**Company size**: Very small. Family-owned business based in Palmetto Bay, FL. No presence on major review platforms. No publicly available employee count or revenue figures; ZoomInfo has a profile but details are behind a paywall.\n    36→\n    37→**Deployment**: Available as cloud-based (monthly per-provider fee), cloud-based revenue-sharing model (percentage of collections plus potential per-FTE charges), or license-based (one-time fee with monthly maintenance, customer or vendor-hosted). Mobile access is supported via RDP connections to dedicated servers.\n    38→\n    39→### Modules & Functionality\n    40→\n    41→Based on vendor website, disclosure pages, and Alignable profile, module though specific sub-features not detailed)\n    59→- Revenue cycle management\n    60→- Billing management (the company originated as a claim adjudication company, and billing/revenue cycle is Direct protocol messaging (via EMR Direct's Interoperability Engine platform, certified 2020)\n    74→- C-CDA document generation and exchange for transitions of care\n    75→- HL7 FHIR API access (Standardized API)\n    76→- Patient portal functionality (e)(1) — though the older disclosure page notes the patient portal involves a third-party component with additional costs\n    77→\n measure data. The CPOE certification for medications, labs, and imaging (a)(1)–(a)(3) confirms these order types are stored in the system.\n    93→\n    94→**Prescribing data**: Electronic prescription data, drug interaction checking data. The (a)(4) certification (drug-drug/drug-allergy checks) confirms medication and allergy data is actively managed.\n    95→\n    96→**Care coordination data**: Transition of care summaries (C-CDA documents), Direct messages for care coordination, referral information (implied by (b)(1)–(b)(2) certification).\n    97→\n    98→**Practice management / billing data**: The vendor's origin as a claim adjudication company and explicit listing of \"revenue cycle management\" and \"billing management\" as core modules indicates the product stores claims data, billing records, payment information, and payer/insurance data. MDVita Analytics' ability to report on \"claim counts, average costs, paid amounts, funding reports, and key expenses\" filtered by insurance confirms insurance/claims data is stored.\n    99→\n   100→**Patient portal data**: Patient-facing data accessible through the portal (e)(1), including the ability to view, download, and transmit health information.\n   101→\n   102→**Public health data**: Immunization data transmitted to registries, syndromic surveillance data — both confirmed by (f)(1) and (f)(2) certification.\n   103→\n   104→**Administrative data**: Provider information, location data, scheduling data (implied by practice management module though not explicitly detailed), and audit logs (required by (d) criteria).\n   105→\n   106→**What's less clear**: The vendor website does not explicitly mention document management/scanning, patient messaging/secure communications (beyond Direct protocol), or appointment scheduling details. The older disclosure page notes additional costs for \"Internet Mailbox\" and \"File Repository\" add-ons, suggesting document storage and secure messaging may be optional components. The nature of the patient portal (third-party vs. integrated) introduces some ambiguity about what patient-generated data is stored in MDVita itself vs. a third-party portal system.\n   107→\n   108→---\n   109→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Founded in 1997 by Martin Gonzalez as a claim adjudication company, the company launched its software division in 2000 with a product called MD2000, a healthcare practice management application. That product evolved into MDVita, their current ONC-certified EHR and practice management suite. The company describes itself as having \"more than 20 years of service in South Florida\" and emphasizes low employee turnover (average tenure of 10 years).\n\nHealth Care 2000 services \"hundreds of medical centers\" according to their website, primarily in South Florida. Their niche is value-based care providers — specifically physicians operating under risk-based contracts with Medicare Advantage plans and other value-driven payment arrangements. Beyond software, the company provides customized financial consulting and data analysis services through in-house healthcare finance professionals. The company has no presence on major software review platforms (G2, Capterra) and appears to be a small regional vendor serving a localized market.\n\n## Product: MDVita\n\nCHPL ID: 11000\nCHPL Product Number: 15.04.04.2904.MDVi.27.02.1.221020\nVersion: 27 (certified October 20, 2022, by Drummond Group)\nSED Intended Users: Family Practice\n\n### What It Is\n\nMDVita is an ONC-certified electronic medical record (EMR) and physician practice management application. It is not a component of a larger product — MDVita is the full product, encompassing both clinical EHR and administrative practice management functionality in a single integrated suite. The product is specifically designed for value-based care providers in primary/family practice settings.\n\nMDVita Analytics is a separately named extension module that provides financial analytics and utilization performance measurement. It appears to be offered as an add-on to the core MDVita product.\n\nThe product has a broad certification profile with 38+ criteria including clinical documentation (a)(1)–(a)(5), (a)(12), (a)(14), transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(2), patient portal/VDT (e)(1), public health reporting (f)(1)–(f)(2), FHIR API (g)(7)–(g)(10), and Direct messaging (h)(1). This is a comprehensive certification for a small vendor.\n\n### Users & Market\n\n**Target users**: Physicians and clinical staff in family/general/primary care practices. The SED testing report indicates the intended user is \"Family Practice.\"\n\n**Customer base**: \"Hundreds of medical centers\" in South Florida, per the vendor website. The product is described as \"a very popular application suite used in South Florida by many health care providers\" (Alignable profile). No specific customer names or case studies are publicly available.\n\n**Clinical setting**: Ambulatory primary care practices, particularly those operating under Medicare Advantage risk-based contracts and value-based payment arrangements. Not hospital-oriented.\n\n**Company size**: Very small. Family-owned business based in Palmetto Bay, FL. No presence on major review platforms. No publicly available employee count or revenue figures; ZoomInfo has a profile but details are behind a paywall.\n\n**Deployment**: Available as cloud-based (monthly per-provider fee), cloud-based revenue-sharing model (percentage of collections plus potential per-FTE charges), or license-based (one-time fee with monthly maintenance, customer or vendor-hosted). Mobile access is supported via RDP connections to dedicated servers.\n\n### Modules & Functionality\n\nBased on vendor website, disclosure pages, and Alignable profile, MDVita includes the following modules and capabilities:\n\n**Electronic Health Records / Clinical**\n- Clinical notes and documentation\n- Patient chart with clinical information\n- Treatment plans\n- Computerized Provider Order Entry (CPOE) for medications, lab orders, and diagnostic imaging\n- Drug-drug and drug-allergy interaction checking\n- Clinical decision support\n- Problem list management\n- Vital signs documentation\n- Medication and allergy management\n- Family health history\n- Patient demographics\n- Patient education resources\n\n**Practice Management**\n- Health care practice management (scheduling, registration — implied by \"practice management\" module though specific sub-features not detailed)\n- Revenue cycle management\n- Billing management (the company originated as a claim adjudication company, and billing/revenue cycle is a core described capability)\n\n**ePrescribe**\n- Electronic prescribing functionality\n\n**Analytics (MDVita Analytics — add-on module)**\n- Financial data reporting and analysis\n- Customizable reports on claim counts, average costs, paid amounts, funding reports, and key expenses\n- Reports filterable by location, patient, provider, insurance, and date\n- Utilization and performance measurement\n- Designed to help manage revenue cycles across multiple lines of business\n\n**Interoperability**\n- Direct protocol messaging (via EMR Direct's Interoperability Engine platform, certified 2020)\n- C-CDA document generation and exchange for transitions of care\n- HL7 FHIR API access (Standardized API)\n- Patient portal functionality (e)(1) — though the older disclosure page notes the patient portal involves a third-party component with additional costs\n\n**Public Health Reporting**\n- Immunization registry transmission (f)(1)\n- Syndromic surveillance reporting (f)(2)\n\n**Quality Measures**\n- Clinical quality measure tracking and reporting\n- QRDA file generation (noted as additional cost)\n- 16 specific clinical quality measures supported per the older disclosure, including diabetes management, cancer screenings, and medication appropriateness\n- 9 clinical quality measures per the current disclosure page\n\n### Data & Content\n\nBased on the described modules and certification criteria, MDVita stores and manages:\n\n**Clinical data**: Patient demographics, medical history, family health history, problem lists, medication lists, allergy lists, vital signs, clinical notes, treatment plans, lab orders and results, diagnostic imaging orders, immunization records, patient education materials provided, and clinical quality measure data. The CPOE certification for medications, labs, and imaging (a)(1)–(a)(3) confirms these order types are stored in the system.\n\n**Prescribing data**: Electronic prescription data, drug interaction checking data. The (a)(4) certification (drug-drug/drug-allergy checks) confirms medication and allergy data is actively managed.\n\n**Care coordination data**: Transition of care summaries (C-CDA documents), Direct messages for care coordination, referral information (implied by (b)(1)–(b)(2) certification).\n\n**Practice management / billing data**: The vendor's origin as a claim adjudication company and explicit listing of \"revenue cycle management\" and \"billing management\" as core modules indicates the product stores claims data, billing records, payment information, and payer/insurance data. MDVita Analytics' ability to report on \"claim counts, average costs, paid amounts, funding reports, and key expenses\" filtered by insurance confirms insurance/claims data is stored.\n\n**Patient portal data**: Patient-facing data accessible through the portal (e)(1), including the ability to view, download, and transmit health information.\n\n**Public health data**: Immunization data transmitted to registries, syndromic surveillance data — both confirmed by (f)(1) and (f)(2) certification.\n\n**Administrative data**: Provider information, location data, scheduling data (implied by practice management module though not explicitly detailed), and audit logs (required by (d) criteria).\n\n**What's less clear**: The vendor website does not explicitly mention document management/scanning, patient messaging/secure communications (beyond Direct protocol), or appointment scheduling details. The older disclosure page notes additional costs for \"Internet Mailbox\" and \"File Repository\" add-ons, suggesting document storage and secure messaging may be optional components. The nature of the patient portal (third-party vs. integrated) introduces some ambiguity about what patient-generated data is stored in MDVita itself vs. a third-party portal system.\n\n---\n","numLines":109,"startLine":1,"totalLines":109}}}

The document itself is dated September 19, 2023 (Guide version 1.2).\n\n## What Was Found\n\nThe PDF is a 28-page EHI Export Data Format specification titled \"MDVITA Electronic Health Information. Export format\" (Guide version 1.2, MDVita version 27). It explicitly states it is written to comply with 170.315(b)(10) and the Information Blocking act.\n\n### Export Format\n\nThe export produces three groups of files:\n\n1. **Raw Data** — Apache Parquet format files (e.g., `Patient.parquet`). This is the structured tabular data.\n2. **SOAP Notes** — Clinical notes exported as individual PDF files (machine-readable, programmatically generated). An index file (`SOAPNotesIndex.parquet`) maps notes to patients. The naming convention is `CareEventID_MemberID.pdf`.\n3. **Documents** — Exported in their original uploaded format (PDF, XML, HTML, CSV, DOC, JPG, etc.). An index file (`DocumentsIndex.parquet`) maps documents to patients. Named by `DocumentID.ext`.\n\nSOAP Notes and Documents are delivered via time-limited Azure Blob Storage URLs (valid 14 days). Reference files (`SOAPNotesReferences_XXX.csv` and `DocumentsReference_XXX.csv`) contain `FileName,FileDownloadURL` columns for automated download.\n\n### Data Files Documented\n\nThe PDF provides field-level documentation for **24 Parquet data files** covering:\n\n| # | File | Domain | Fields |\n|---|------|--------|--------|\n| 1 | Patients | Demographics | 27 fields — MemberID, DOB, gender, name, SSN, address, employer, race, ethnicity, language, transport needs, death info |\n| 2 | ProviderNetwork | External providers | 18 fields — PhysID, NPI, taxonomy, name, address, DEA, UPIN, TaxID |\n| 3 | ProviderPCPs | In-house providers | 18 fields — same structure as ProviderNetwork but for in-house PCPs |\n| 4 | Locations | Service locations | 14 fields — NPI, TaxID, name, address, CLIA number, appointment interval |\n| 5 | PatientPlans | Insurance/plans | 21 fields — plan enrollment, insurance company, LOB, copay amounts, effective/term dates |\n| 6 | Appointments | Scheduling | 18 fields — date/time, provider, status, transportation details, special needs |\n| 7 | SOAPNotesIndex | Clinical notes index | 9 fields — CareEventID, service date, attending physician, subject, comments |\n| 8 | Orders | Clinical orders | 11 fields — referrals, tests, lab orders, text instructions, results |\n| 9 | ProblemList | Diagnoses | 9 fields — ICD codes (ICD9/ICD10/SNOMED), status (active/inactive/resolved), dates |\n| 10 | Allergies | Allergies | 9 fields — name, class (drug/environmental/substance), NDC/SNOMED/UNII codes, status |\n| 11 | MedicationList | Medications | 20 fields — brand/generic name, strength, NDC, SIG, route, frequency, dosage |\n| 12 | ProcedureList | Procedures | 5 fields — CPT code, dates |\n| 13 | DocumentsIndex | Documents index | 12 fields — name, type, binder, service date, parent binder |\n| 14 | LabResults | Lab results | 18 fields — ordering provider, SNOMED codes, result values, reference ranges, status |\n| 15 | Claims | Claims/encounters | 55+ fields — claim type, billing provider, diagnoses, procedures with charges, modifiers, EPSDT, place of service, NDC drug info |\n| 16 | Referrals | Referrals | 35+ fields — referral type/urgency, certification, authorization, service dates, diagnosis codes, clinical notes status |\n| 17 | Emails | Internal messages | 11 fields — activity threads, patient association, name, unit of measure, two value columns |\n| 20 | DocumentSignatures | Signature audit | 4 fields — document ID, signed date, user login |\n| 21 | ClaimInsurancePayments | Payer payments/EOBs | 23 |\n| 23 | MemberPayments | Patient payments | 12 fields — payment amount, type, check number, e-payment details, reversal |\n| 24 | DocumentAnnotations | Document annotations | 5 fields — resolution notes, annotation body, dates |\n\nEach file is documented with column name, data type (Numeric, String, DateTime, Boolean, Date), and a description. Coded fields include possible values (e.g., gender codes, order types, claim types, referral urgency levels, result statuses).\n\n### Key Design Choices\n\n- **Parquet format** is an unusual and technically strong choice — it's a columnar binary format with embedded schema, widely supported by data engineering tools (Python/pandas, R, Spark, DuckDB). It preserves data types natively.\n- **Documents delivered by reference** via time-limited Azure Blob URLs is a practical approach for potentially large document sets.\n- **Relationships are documented**: The data dictionary consistently cross-references files (e.g., \"See Patients data file\", \"See ProviderPCPs data file\") and identifies join keys (MemberID/PatientID, CareEventID, MemberPlanID, PhysID, etc.).\n- The document notes that PatientID and MemberID are used \"indistinctively\" as the same patient account identifier.\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\nThis is a genuinely comprehensive (b)(10) export that goes well beyond the USCDI clinical core. It covers:\n\n**Clearly covered:**\n- Patient demographics (comprehensive — name, DOB, SSN, address, employer, race, ethnicity, language, transport needs, death info)\n- Insurance/plan enrollment with copay details and line of business\n- Appointments with transportation logistics and special needs\n- Clinical notes (SOAP Notes as PDFs + structured index)\n- Orders (referrals, tests, labs, text instructions)\n- Problem lists with ICD9/ICD10/SNOMED codes and status tracking\n- Allergies with NDC/SNOMED/UNII codes\n- Medications with full prescription detail (NDC, SIG, route, frequency, dosage)\n- Procedures (CPT-coded)\n- Lab results with SNOMED-coded observations and reference ranges\n- Documents in original format with annotations\n- Claims and encounters (extremely detailed — 55+ fields including billing provider info, procedure-level charges, modifiers, place of service, drug NDC, EPSDT)\n- Referrals with full authorization/certification detail\n- Immunizations with CVX codes and manufacturer info\n- Vital signs\n- Document signatures (audit trail)\n- Insurance payments and EOBs (check-level and procedure-level detail)\n- Patient charges and payments (including electronic payment details and reversals)\n- Internal emails/messages between MDVita users about patients\n\n**Potentially missing or unclear:**\n- **Audit logs** — There is a DocumentSignatures file tracking document review events, but no general system audit log (login events, record access, modifications). The (d) certification criteria require audit logging, so this data exists in the system but may not be included in the export.\n- **Clinical decision support alerts/interactions** — Drug-drug and drug-allergy interaction checking is a certified feature, but alert history is not explicitly in the export.\n- **Quality measure data** — The product supports CQM tracking and QRDA generation, but quality measure results are not an explicit export file.\n- **E-prescribing transaction history** — Medications are exported but specific e-prescribing transmission logs are not mentioned.\n- **Patient portal activity** — The product has a patient portal (with third-party component), but portal-specific activity data is not in the export.\n- **Scheduling templates/configuration** — While appointments are exported, the scheduling configuration (provider schedules, appointment types) is not.\n\nOverall, the coverage is strong. The export captures the core clinical record, the full billing/financial lifecycle (claims, insurance payments, patient charges, patient payments), referral management, and internal communications. This is clearly a purpose-built (b)(10) export, not a repurposed FHIR API.\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\n- **Format**: Apache Parquet for structured data, PDF for clinical notes, original format for uploaded documents. CSV reference files for document download URLs.\n- **Standard**: Parquet is a well-established open-source columnar storage format (Apache Foundation). It is not a healthcare-specific standard but is a strong technical choice for bulk data export — it preserves data types, is self-describing, and is efficiently queryable.\n- **Not FHIR**: This is explicitly a database-level export, not a FHIR-based export. This is appropriate given the breadth of data (billing, referral authorization, internal messaging) that doesn't map cleanly to FHIR resources.\n- **Relationships**: Cross-file references are documented through shared identifiers (MemberID, CareEventID, PhysID, MemberPlanID, etc.). A third party could reconstruct the patient record by joining across these files.\n- **Terminology**: The export uses standard code systems where applicable — ICD-9/ICD-10/SNOMED for diagnoses, CPT for procedures, NDC for drugs, CVX for vaccines, NPI for providers — while using internal codes for operational fields.\n\nThe format is well-suited to the data. A developer with Parquet tooling could load and query this export straightforwardly.\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n- **Readable and well-organized**: Each data file gets its own numbered section (sections 3–26) with a consistent table format of Column Name, Data Type, and Description.\n- **Field-level definitions**: Every column in every file is documented with a name, data type, and description.\n- **Coded values documented**: Where fields have enumerated values, the possible values and their meanings are listed (e.g., gender codes, order types, claim types, referral urgency, result statuses, accident codes, bill frequency codes, EPSDT conditions, release of medical records codes, certification types, payment action codes).\n- **Cross-references**: Relationships between files are explicitly noted (\"See Patients data file\", \"See ProviderPCPs data file\").\n- **No sample data**: There are no example Parquet files or sample records included. The Azure Blob URL examples in the document use illustrative but non-functional URLs.\n- **No export instructions**: The document directs users to \"the MDVita User Guide for instructions how to schedule an EHI export\" which is available within the application. The user guide for triggering the export is not publicly available.\n- **Versioned**: Guide version 1.2, dated September 2023, for MDVita version 27. The PDF file itself was last modified January 12, 2024.\n\nA developer could implement an import of this data based on this documentation. The Parquet format is self-describing (column names and types are embedded), so the documentation serves as a human-readable reference rather than the sole schema source.\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\n- **Granularity**: Field-level documentation with column names, data types, and descriptions for all 24 data files.\n- **Data types**: Specified for every field (Numeric, String, DateTime, Boolean, Date).\n- **Value sets**: Coded fields include enumerated values with descriptions.\n- **Relationships**: Join keys and cross-file references are documented.\n- **Cardinality**: Not explicitly documented (no mention of required vs. optional fields, or one-to-many relationships), though the structure implies cardinality (e.g., Claims has procedure-level fields suggesting claim-line detail is denormalized into the claim record).\n- **No formal schema**: There is no separate machine-readable schema file (e.g., JSON Schema, Avro schema). However, since Parquet files embed their schema, the actual export files would be self-describing.\n- **No change history**: The document has a version number (1.2) but no changelog.\n\n## Access Summary\n- Final URL (after redirects): https://www.hc2000inc.com/Pages/MDVita_EHR_EHI_DataFormat.pdf\n- Status: found\n- Required browser: no\n- Navigation complexity: direct_link\n- Anti-bot issues: none\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n\nNone. Export format\" (Guide version 1.2, MDVita version 27). It explicitly states it is written to comply with 170.315(b)(10) and the Information Blocking act.\n\n### Export Format\n\nThe export produces three groups of files:\n\n1. **Raw Data** — Apache Parquet format files (e.g., `Patient.parquet`). This is the structured tabular data.\n2. **SOAP Notes** — Clinical notes exported as individual PDF files (machine-readable, programmatically generated). An index file (`SOAPNotesIndex.parquet`) maps notes to patients. The naming convention is `CareEventID_MemberID.pdf`.\n3. **Documents** — Exported in their original uploaded format (PDF, XML, HTML, CSV, DOC, JPG, etc.). An index file (`DocumentsIndex.parquet`) maps documents to patients. Named by `DocumentID.ext`.\n\nSOAP Notes and Documents are delivered via time-limited Azure Blob Storage URLs (valid 14 days). Reference files (`SOAPNotesReferences_XXX.csv` and `DocumentsReference_XXX.csv`) contain `FileName,FileDownloadURL` columns for automated download.\n\n### Data Files Documented\n\nThe PDF provides field-level documentation for **24 Parquet data files** covering:\n\n| # | File | Domain | Fields |\n|---|------|--------|--------|\n| 1 | Patients | Demographics | 27 fields — MemberID, DOB, gender, name, SSN, address, employer, race, ethnicity, language, transport needs, death info |\n| 2 | ProviderNetwork | External providers | 18 fields — PhysID, NPI, taxonomy, name, address, DEA, UPIN, TaxID |\n| 3 | ProviderPCPs | In-house providers | 18 fields — same structure as ProviderNetwork but for in-house PCPs |\n| 4 | Locations | Service locations | 14 fields — NPI, TaxID, name, address, CLIA comments |\n| 8 | Orders | Clinical orders | 11 fields — referrals, tests, lab orders, text instructions, results |\n| 9 | ProblemList | Diagnoses | 9 fields — ICD codes (ICD9/ICD10/SNOMED), status (active/inactive/resolved), dates |\n| 10 | Allergies | Allergies | 9 fields — name, class (drug/environmental/substance), NDC/SNOMED/UNII codes, status |\n| 11 | MedicationList | Medications | 20 fields — brand/generic name, strength, NDC, SIG, route, frequency, dosage |\n| 12 | ProcedureList | Procedures | 5 fields — CPT code, dates |\n| 13 | DocumentsIndex | Documents index | 12 fields — name, type, binder, service date, parent binder |\n| 14 | LabResults | Lab results | 18 fields — ordering provider, SNOMED codes, result values, reference ranges, status |\n| 15 | Claims | Claims/encounters | 55+ fields — claim type, billing provider, diagnoses, procedures with charges, modifiers, EPSDT, place of service, NDC drug info |\n| 16 | Referrals | Referrals | 35+ fields — referral type/urgency, certification, authorization, service dates, diagnosis codes, clinical notes status |\n| 17 | Emails | Internal messages | 11 fields — activity threads, patient association, body, importance |\n| 18 | Immunizations | Immunizations | 17 fields — CVX code, vaccine name, manufacturer, lot, administered amount, refusal reason |\n| 19 | Vitals | Vital signs | 7 fields — vital name, unit of measure, two value columns |\n| 20 | DocumentSignatures | Signature audit | 4 fields — document ID, signed date, user login |\n| 21 | ClaimInsurancePayments | Payer payments/EOBs | 23 fields — check info, CPT paid amounts, allowed amounts, copay, deductible, coinsurance, reason codes |\n| 22 | MemberCharges | Patient charges | 8 fields — charge amount, date, reason, reversal date |\n| 23 | MemberPayments | Patient payments | 12 fields — payment amount, type, check number, e-payment details, reversal |\n| 24 | DocumentAnnotations | Document annotations | 5 fields — resolution notes, annotation body, dates |\n\nEach file is documented with column name, data type (Numeric, String, DateTime, Boolean, Date), and a description. Coded fields include possible values (e.g., gender codes, order types, claim types, referral urgency levels, result statuses).\n\n### Key Design Choices\n\n- **Parquet format** is an unusual and technically strong choice — it's a columnar binary format with embedded schema, widely supported by data engineering tools (Python/pandas, R, Spark, DuckDB). It preserves data types natively.\n- **Documents delivered by reference** via time-limited Azure Blob URLs is a practical approach for potentially large document sets.\n- **Relationships are documented**: The data dictionary consistently cross-references files (e.g., \"See Patients data file\", \"See ProviderPCPs data file\") and identifies join keys (MemberID/PatientID, CareEventID, MemberPlanID, PhysID, etc.).\n- The document notes that PatientID and MemberID are used \"indistinctively\" as the same patient account identifier.\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\nThis is a genuinely comprehensive (b)(10) export that goes well beyond the USCDI clinical core. It covers:\n\n**Clearly covered:**\n- Patient demographics (comprehensive — name, DOB, SSN, address, employer, race, ethnicity, language, transport needs, death info)\n- Insurance/plan enrollment with copay details and line of business\n- Appointments with transportation logistics and special needs\n- Clinical notes (SOAP Notes as PDFs + structured index)\n- Orders (referrals, tests, labs, text instructions)\n- Problem lists with ICD9/ICD10/SNOMED codes and status tracking\n- Allergies with NDC/SNOMED/UNII codes\n- Medications with full prescription detail (NDC, SIG, route, frequency, dosage)\n- Procedures (CPT-coded)\n- Lab results with SNOMED-coded observations and reference ranges\n- Documents in original format with annotations\n- Claims and encounters (extremely detailed — 55+ fields including billing provider info, procedure-level charges, modifiers, place of service, drug NDC, EPSDT)\n- Referrals with full authorization/certification detail\n- Immunizations with CVX codes and manufacturer info\n- Vital signs\n- Document signatures (audit trail)\n- Insurance payments and EOBs (check-level and procedure-level detail)\n- Patient charges and payments (including electronic payment details and reversals)\n- Internal emails/messages between MDVita users about patients\n\n**Potentially missing or unclear:**\n- **Audit logs** — There is a DocumentSignatures file tracking document review events, but no general system audit log (login events, record access, modifications). The (d) certification criteria require audit logging, so this data exists in the system but may not be included in the export.\n- **Clinical decision support alerts/interactions** — Drug-drug and drug-allergy interaction checking is a certified feature, but alert history is not explicitly in the export.\n- **Quality measure data** — The product supports CQM tracking and QRDA generation, but quality measure results are not an explicit export file.\n- **E-prescribing transaction history** — Medications are exported but specific e-prescribing transmission logs are not mentioned.\n- **Patient portal activity** — The product has a patient portal (with third-party component), but portal-specific activity data is not in the export.\n- **Scheduling templates/configuration** — While appointments are exported, the scheduling configuration (provider schedules, appointment types) is not.\n\nOverall, the coverage is strong. The export captures the core clinical record, the full billing/financial lifecycle (claims, insurance payments, patient charges, patient payments), referral management, and internal communications. This is clearly a purpose-built (b)(10) export, not a repurposed FHIR API.\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\n- **Format**: Apache Parquet for structured data, PDF for clinical notes, original format for uploaded documents. CSV reference files for document download URLs.\n- **Standard**: Parquet is a well-established open-source columnar storage format (Apache Foundation). It is not a healthcare-specific standard but is a strong technical choice for bulk data export — it preserves data types, is self-describing, and is efficiently queryable.\n- **Not FHIR**: This is explicitly a database-level export, not a FHIR-based export. This is appropriate given the breadth of data (billing, referral authorization, internal messaging) that doesn't map cleanly to FHIR resources.\n- **Relationships**: Cross-file references are documented through shared identifiers (MemberID, CareEventID, PhysID, MemberPlanID, etc.). A third party could reconstruct the patient record by joining across these files.\n- **Terminology**: The export uses standard code systems where applicable — ICD-9/ICD-10/SNOMED for diagnoses, CPT for procedures, NDC for drugs, CVX for vaccines, NPI for providers — while using internal codes for operational fields.\n\nThe format is well-suited to the data. A developer with Parquet tooling could load and query this export straightforwardly.\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n- **Readable and well-organized**: Each data file gets its own numbered section (sections 3–26) with a consistent table format of Column Name, Data Type, and Description.\n- **Field-level definitions**: Every column in every file is documented with a name, data type, and description.\n- **Coded values documented**: Where fields have enumerated values, the possible values and their meanings are listed (e.g., gender codes, order types, claim types, referral urgency, result statuses, accident codes, bill frequency codes, EPSDT conditions, release of medical records codes, certification types, payment action codes).\n- **Cross-references**: Relationships between files are explicitly noted (\"See Patients data file\", \"See ProviderPCPs data file\").\n- **No sample data**: There are no example Parquet files or sample records included. The Azure Blob URL examples in the document use illustrative but non-functional URLs.\n- **No export instructions**: The document directs users to \"the MDVita User Guide for instructions how to schedule an EHI export\" which is available within the application. The user guide for triggering the export is not publicly available.\n- **Versioned**: Guide version 1.2, dated September 2023, for MDVita version 27. The PDF file itself was last modified January 12, 2024.\n\nA developer could implement an import of this data based on this documentation. The Parquet format is self-describing (column names and types are embedded), so the documentation serves as a human-readable reference rather than the sole schema source.\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\n- **Granularity**: Field-level documentation with column names, data types, and descriptions for all 24 data files.\n- **Data types**: Specified for every field (Numeric, String, DateTime, Boolean, Date).\n- **Value sets**: Coded fields include enumerated values with descriptions.\n- **Relationships**: Join keys and cross-file references are documented.\n- **Cardinality**: Not explicitly documented (no mention of required vs. optional fields, or one-to-many relationships), though the structure implies cardinality (e.g., Claims has procedure-level fields suggesting claim-line detail is denormalized into the claim record).\n- **No formal schema**: There is no separate machine-readable schema file (e.g., JSON Schema, Avro schema).
